d="M0 0h12v12H0z" fill="#fff"></path></clippath></defs></svg></span></div>Newsweek is a Trust Project member<div class="Icon_container__6WLaL Icon_sm__K8KED"><span aria-hidden="true" class="Icon_root__5T0Zw height_root__6FnI_ height_--type-literal__T2ZG2" style="--rs-h-s:100%"><svg fill="none" focusable="false" height="12" viewbox="0 0 12 12" width="12" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g clip-path="url(#clip0_2548_23033)"><path d="M5.25 2V3H1.5V10.5H9V6.75H10V11.5H0.5V2H5.25ZM11.5 5H10.5V2.20703L5.35352 7.35352L4.64648 6.64648L9.79297 1.5H7V0.5H11.5V5Z" fill="#68645A"></path></g><defs><clippath id="clip0_2548_23033"><rect fill="white" height="12" width="12"></rect></clippath></defs></svg></span></div></a></div></div></div></div><div class="ArticleTwoColumnLayout_contentWrapper__D_Fms"><article class="PostContent_articleBody__FR8Mb"><p class="Paragraph_blockParagraph__I2kr4">As Donald Trump continues to fight against a congressional subpoena from House Democrats for financial records, he will now have to face the Obama-nominated judge Republicans refused to consider for the Supreme Court.</p><p class="Paragraph_blockParagraph__I2kr4">Merrick Garland is currently the chief judge at the D.C. Circuit Court of Appeals, where President Trump's legal battle will head next as the president's attorneys attempt to reverse the earlier court ruling in favor of Congress.</p><p class="Paragraph_blockParagraph__I2kr4">Garland was nominated to the Supreme Court by President Barack Obama in 2016 following the death of Associate Justice Antonin Scalia. But congressional Republicans stonewalled his nomination process until after the election, arguing that the incoming president should be the one to nominate a judge to the lifelong position.</p><p class="Paragraph_blockParagraph__I2kr4">After Trump was elected, he quickly nominated conservative Justice Neil Gorsuch to the high court. As a result, Garland resumed his position as chief judge of the nation's most important federal appeals court, where he has served since 1997.</p><p class="Paragraph_blockParagraph__I2kr4">The irony of the situation was highlighted by legal analysts and political commentators on Twitter.</p><p class="Paragraph_blockParagraph__I2kr4">"I wonder who the chief judge is in the circuit where all of the fights between Congress and Trump will play out and whether he cares about partisan norm-busting. Oh that's right.... It's some guy named Merrick Garland," Matthew Miller, a former spokesman at the Department of Justice, tweeted.</p><p class="Paragraph_blockParagraph__I2kr4">Dena Grayson, a former Democratic candidate for Congress, wrote on Twitter: "LOL… guess who serves as the chief judge in the circuit court where the legal appeals between Congress and @realDonaldTrump will be heard?"</p><div class="Embed_embedWrapper__rftvU embed-loading"><div class="embed-loading-content"><p>Loading <!-- -->twitter<!-- --> content...</p></div></div><p class="Paragraph_blockParagraph__I2kr4">In late April, Senate Majority Leader Mitch McConnell reignited the debate surrounding Garland's failed nomination when he signed a T-shirt featuring the judge's face with the quote "Gone but not forgotten."</p><p class="Paragraph_blockParagraph__I2kr4">On Monday, U.S. District Court Judge Amit Mehta ruled that Congress is well within its rights to request financial records as part of an investigation into potentially illegal conduct of a sitting president.</p><p class="Paragraph_blockParagraph__I2kr4">The House Oversight and Reform Committee has requested documents from Mazars USA, an accounting firm for the president and the Trump Organization. Democrats are looking for eight years of Trump's financial records.</p><p class="Paragraph_blockParagraph__I2kr4">Shortly after Mehta's ruling, Trump attorney Jay Sekulow said that his team "will be filing a timely notice of appeal to the D.C. Circuit Court of Appeals." Sekulow also called the ruling "totally wrong" and "ridiculous."</p><p class="Paragraph_blockParagraph__I2kr4">In a tweet on Monday, Trump slammed Democrats for investigating his finances instead of "looking into all of the crimes committed by Crooked Hillary and the phony Russia investigation."</p><div class="ImageBlock_container__ioAu0"><div class="ImageBlock_imageContainer__OPxoe" style="padding-bottom:66.6667%"><img alt="merrick garland chief judge trump financial records appeal" caption="Chief United States Circuit Judge of the United States Court of Appeals for the District of Columbia Circuit Merrick Garland (center) attends the investiture ceremony for U.S. District Judge Trevor N. McFadden, at the U.S. District Court in Washington, D.C., on April 13, 2018." clicktodisplay="false" credit="Alex Wong/Getty Images" data-nimg="1" decoding="async" fetchpriority="auto" height="396" id="7431525" loading="lazy" showcredit="true" sourcealt="" sources="[]" src="https://assets.newsweek.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/1431525-merrick-garland-chief-judge-trump-financial-records-appeal.jpg?w=1200&amp;quality=75&amp;webp=1" The investigation into Ramos\\u2019s death continues.\\u00a0\\n\\n\\n\\nWhat To Know\u0026nbsp;\\n\\n\\n\\nRamos\u0026#8217;s body was found on December 12, 1989. She had been stabbed multiple times and left nude on Old Temple Bar Road in Mohave County, about 50 miles south of Las Vegas. Decades passed before she was identified. \\u00a0\\n\\n\\n\\nIn 2022, Mohave County investigators matched fingerprints from the unidentified woman to a shoplifting arrest made in Bakersfield, California, for \\u201cMaria Ortiz.\\u201d\\u00a0Investigators said Maria Ortiz was an alias used by Marina Ramos.\\u00a0\\n\\n\\n\\nThe last time Ramos was seen, she was with her two daughters, 2-month-old Jasmin and 14-month-old Elizabeth, according to officials.\\u00a0\\n\\n\\n\\nTwo days after Ramos\u0026#8217;s body was discovered, a passerby in Oxnard heard crying inside a park restroom. He asked a woman to check the bathroom, where she found two babies alone and abandoned on the floor. The girls\\u2019 identities remained unknown, and they were ultimately placed in foster care and adopted together by a couple in Ventura County.\\u00a0\\n\\n\\n\\nIn August of this year, DNA tests submitted by family members resulted in a high-probability match. Further investigation confirmed the adopted women, now known as Melissa and Tina, are Elizabeth Ramos and Jasmin Ramos.\u0026nbsp;\\n\\n\\n\\nTina and Melissa were identified as Jasmin Ramos and Elizabeth Ramos, daughters of Marina Ramos, nearly 36 years after Marina was killed. years.\\n\\n\\n\\nWhy It Matters\\n\\n\\n\\nSince January 2023, there have been near-consistent increases in the price of\\u00a0a single First-Class stamp. The USPS decides around every six months, usually in January and July, whether to raise prices for consumers.\\n\\n\\n\\nWhat To Know\\n\\n\\n\\nIn a press release issued on September 24, the Postal Service confirmed that a recommendation by Postmaster General David Steiner not to raise prices in January 2026 for numerous products had been accepted by USPS governors.\\n\\n\\n\\n\u0026#8220;The price of a stamp to mail a 1-ounce single-piece First-Class letter will not increase in early 2026,\u0026#8221; the release reads. Two years later, doctors confirmed Cockayne syndrome (CS)\\u2014a disorder estimated to affect fewer than 5,000 people in the U.S.\\n\\n\\n\\nThe condition causes short stature, premature aging, severe photosensitivity, and learning difficulties, according  to the National Organization for Rare Disorders (NORD).\\n\\n\\n\\n\\u201cIt is basically killing his body slowly but rapidly compared to everyone else,\\u201d his mom Tarah, 44, who lives in Asheville, North Carolina, told Newsweek.\\n\\n\\n\\nTristan sitting in a pushchair and smiling with his mom Tarah. Provided by Tarah Burrell.\\n\\n\\n\\nLiving With a Rare Condition\\n\\n\\n\\nNow aged 21, Tristan stands 4ft 4in and weighs 63lbs. But Burrell sensed the diagnosis was wrong.\\n\\n\\n\\n\\u201cAs a toddler, Tristan presented with tremors throughout his body if he would get too hot or too cold,\\u201d she recalled. \\u201cThis indicated that he had a myelin deficiency. His hands still tremor to this day, as do his feet and legs.\\u201d\\n\\n\\n\\nDue to his speech delay and borderline impairment, doctors initially considered a diagnosis of Autism Spectrum Disorder (ASD).\\n\\n\\n\\n\\u201cTristan also always burned easily, as children and adults with CS are extremely sensitive to sunlight,\\u201d she added.\\n\\n\\n\\nWatching Siblings Grow Up\\n\\n\\n\\n(L-R) Tristan, twin brothers Luke and Landon, both 18, Ava, 16, hugging mom Tarah and Tristan\u0026#8217;s step dad.\\n\\n\\n\\nThe mom-of-five said her son\\u2019s fatal diagnosis is especially painful as she watches her other children\\u2014Luke and Landon, both 18, Ava, 16, and Josephine, six\\u2014grow and thrive.\\n\\n\\n\\n\\u201cIt was a shock watching the twins grow as it showed me how it was supposed to be,\\u201d she said. \\u201cThey are like grown men next to him, Ava is taller, and Josephine is the only one that is smaller at this point.\\n\\n\\n\\n\\u201cHe is the older brother, but he is more like the youngest. The boys started to mature at 12, and their roles switched.\\n\\n\\n\\n\\u201cIt is emotionally the hardest thing; Tristan has always been a little kid. On a good day, he is hilarious and goofy\\u2014he loves making people laugh. But other times he can be frustrated and grumpy. He just doesn\\u2019t understand the word \\u2018no\\u2019 and will get upset, though he can just as easily bounce back. In many ways, he\\u2019s very much like a toddler.\\u201d\\n\\n\\n\\nCockayne Syndrome Cause\\n\\n\\n\\nNORD explains the disease is caused by changes in genetic material (DNA). Burrell and her ex-partner were unaware they were both carriers as they didn\u0026#8217;t show any symptoms. The condition is so rare it is not checked for during pregnancy.\\n\\n\\n\\nAccording to NORD, if both biological parents are carriers, there is a 25 percent chance their child inherits both copies of the mutated gene and is affected, and a 50 percent chance the child inherits only one copy and becomes a carrier.\\n\\n\\n\\nThe Challenges Ahead\\n\\n\\n\\nRecently, Burrell has noticed her son\\u2019s muscles wasting away, and he can no longer ride a bike.\\n\\n\\n\\n\\u201cI constantly feel like I have a dark cloud that never clears above me\\u2014it\\u2019s always there and never going away,\\u201d Burrell said.\\n\\n\\n\\nPatients with Cockayne Syndrome often have difficulty feeding due to severe reflux, poor oral intake, and rapid muscle loss, sometimes requiring gastrostomy tubes.\\n\\n\\n\\nIn July, Burrell posted a video of Tristan on TikTok (@tmcispoetry) stating he\\u2019s \\u201cnow having trouble swallowing which means the disease is progressing.\\u201d\\n\\n\\n\\n\\u201cWe are fortunate he can do things like playing games,\\u201d she said. \\u201cHe answers a bit slower, and he can\\u2019t cognitively remember things we do in everyday life. You must ask him if he has brushed his teeth and I have to instruct him when he is in the bath and help him.\\n\\n\\n\\n\\u201cIt is awful\\u2014there\\u2019s only so much I can do. It is scary.\\u201d\\n\\n\\n\\nReferences\\n\\n\\n\\nKarikkineth, A. C., Scheibye-Knudsen, M., Fivenson, E., Croteau, D. L., \u0026amp; Bohr, V. A. (2017). Rollins said.\",\"articleBody\":\"The U.S. Department of Agriculture (USDA) is moving to tighten requirements for retailers that participate in the Supplemental Nutrition Assistance Program (SNAP) with a view to expanding access to healthier foods and cracking down on fraud.\\n\\n\\n\\nAgriculture Secretary Brooke L. Rollins announced the proposal this week, saying it reflects the department\\u2019s commitment to safeguarding both participants and taxpayers. \\n\\n\\n\\n\u0026#8220;Retailers participating in SNAP need to sell real food, plain and simple,\u0026#8221; Rollins said. \u0026#8220;Right now, the bar for stocking food as a SNAP retailer is far too low, allowing people to game the system and leaving vulnerable Americans without healthy food options.\u0026#8221;\\n\\n\\n\\nWhy It Matters\\n\\n\\n\\nSNAP benefits are distributed to around 42 million low- and no-income recipients across the country to help them buy groceries. They can use their benefits at participating retailers. According to the USDA, there are nearly 266,000 retailers processing an estimated $96 billion in SNAP benefits annually,\\n\\n\\n\\nWhat To Know\\n\\n\\n\\nAs it stands, SNAP-approved retailers must carry three varieties of food in each of four staple food groups: dairy, protein, grain, and fruits and vegetables. That means a total of 12 foods are required. The proposed changes would increase that threshold significantly. Retailers would have to stock at least seven different items in each staple category, more than doubling the number of food options for participants.\\n\\n\\n\\nThe USDA also plans to:\\n\\n\\n\\n\\nClose loopholes that currently allow some snack foods to count as staples. This does not mean they would no longer be purchasable using SNAP benefits, rather that they would be reclassified for retailers.\\n\\n\\n\\nSimplify how foods are classified, making requirements easier to understand for retailers and easier to enforce for USDA\\u2019s Food and Nutrition Service (FNS).\\n\\n\\n\\n\\nChicago\\u2014Circa April 2022: SNAP and EBT Accepted here sign.\\n\\n\\n\\nThe USDA argues that the existing minimum stocking rules have left the program more vulnerable to misuse. Retailers that are not primarily in the food business have been able to accept SNAP benefits.\\n\\n\\n\\nThe department said that \u0026#8220;no amount of fraud will be tolerated.\u0026#8221; It said the new proposal is designed to ensure the program supports stores that provide real food rather than cashing \u0026#8220;in on taxpayer-funded benefits.\u0026#8221;\\n\\n\\n\\nThe USDA said the initiative is part of a broader effort to redirect SNAP toward better nutrition and to combat chronic disease. Beyond tightening stocking rules, the department has also approved waivers in 12 states that allow certain unhealthy foods to be excluded from SNAP purchases.\\n\\n\\n\\nWhat People Are Saying\\n\\n\\n\\nRollins said: \u0026#8220;These common-sense changes are designed to minimize benefit trafficking and skimming, among other fraudulent activities, while making more nutritious foods available to families who rely on the program. With these principles in mind, NGA supports the U.S. Department of Agriculture\\u2019s efforts to strengthen stocking requirements for SNAP retailers.
